When we connected the phone to the internet, the mobile revolution was born. Today, our foundational technologies enable the mobile ecosystem and are found in every 3G, 4G and 5G smartphone. We bring the benefits of mobile to new industries, including automotive, the internet of things, and computing, and are leading the way to a world where everything and everyone can communicate and interact seamlessly.\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/p>\n\u003cp>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>Qualcomm Incorporated includes our licensing business, QTL, and the vast majority of our patent portfolio. Qualcomm Technologies, Inc., a subsidiary of Qualcomm Incorporated, operates, along with its subsidiaries, substantially all of our engineering, research and development functions, and substantially all of our products and services businesses, including our QCT semiconductor business.\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/p>\n"}]],"prReleaseLocation":["SAN DIEGO"],"prClickThrough":[false],"publishDate":[1615897800],"pressNote":[true],"references":[]},"analytics":{"countryCode":"us","languageCode":"en","siteBrand":"qualcomm","siteName":"qualcomm","siteRegion":"north-america","siteTier":"region"},"section":{"name":"Press Releases","machineName":"press_release","path":"news/releases","colorName":"blue"},"css":[]},"813129":{"nid":"813129","attributes":{"nid":"813129","type":"blog","title":"Journey to Mars: How our collaboration with Jet Propulsion Laboratory fostered innovation [video]","created":"1615996800","changed":"1615996802","language":"und","url":"/news/onq/2021/03/17/journey-mars-how-our-collaboration-jet-propulsion-laboratory-fostered-innovation"},"type":"blog","title":"Journey to Mars: How our collaboration with Jet Propulsion Laboratory fostered innovation [video]","created":"1615996800","changed":"1615996802","language":"und","id":"813129","entityType":"node","path":"/news/onq/2021/03/17/journey-mars-how-our-collaboration-jet-propulsion-laboratory-fostered-innovation","url":"/news/onq/2021/03/17/journey-mars-how-our-collaboration-jet-propulsion-laboratory-fostered-innovation","fields":{"body":[[{"type":"image","image":"https://www.qualcomm.com/sites/ember/files/styles/optimize/public/blog/managed-images/qc_mars_header_688x444.png?itok=MHiQEPvf","class":"inline","description":"Image credit: NASA/JPL-Caltech","title":"","alt":"","width":688,"height":444},{"type":"html","value":"\u003cp>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">Inventing breakthrough technologies that have positive impact and meet society’s needs is at our core. We also believe in fostering collaborations that drive innovation. That’s why Qualcomm Technologies, which includes Qualcomm Government Technologies and Qualcomm CDMA Technologies, is pleased to share the hard work we’ve been doing with \u003c/span>\u003ca href=\"https://www.jpl.nasa.gov/who-we-are\">\u003cspan>\u003cspan>NASA Jet Propulsion Labs (JPL)\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/a>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\"> in developing technologies and solutions that power the Mars helicopter, \u003c/span>\u003cw:sdt id=\"1847124796\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_10\">\u003ca href=\"https://www.nasa.gov/feature/jpl/nasa-s-mars-helicopter-reports-in\">\u003ci>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>Ingenuity\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/i>\u003c/a>\u003c/w:sdt>\u003ci>\u003cu>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">\u003cspan>,\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/u>\u003c/i> \u003cw:sdt id=\"-732536596\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_11\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">to prepare for the first powered flight on another planet.\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/p>\n\u003cp>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">The Mars helicopter project has been in development since 2014 and is the culmination of rigorous testing and innovation. The project is meant to be a technology demonstration by JPL to showcase how autonomous flight can expand the horizon of space exploration, research, and data\u003c/span>\u003cw:sdt id=\"1610544006\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_13\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003cw:sdt id=\"-1187675835\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_14\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\"> for future missions and designs. No technical detail would be too small to consider, including the processor that would be responsible for the helicopter’s operation.\u003c/span>\u003cw:sdt id=\"383460742\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_16\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\"> When JPL approached us about testing and expanding the autonomous capabilities of Ingenuity using products from \u003c/span>\u003cw:sdt id=\"-1331903821\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_17\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">Qualcomm Technologies, we were thrilled to share in their team’s vision. \u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/p>\n\u003ch3>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">The challenges of first-ever space flight\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/h3>\n\u003cp>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">The rigors of space pose unique challenges to operating a helicopter on Mars — challenges our \u003c/span>\u003ca href=\"/news/onq/2015/09/10/first-public-demo-snapdragon-flight-robotics-dev-platform-one-worlds-smallest-4k\">\u003cspan>\u003cspan>Qualcomm Flight Platform\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/a>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">, is capable of addressing. The main hurdle is operation itself; due to signals taking minutes to arrive, controlling a helicopter via remote control in real time is impossible. The helicopter must instead receive commands for autonomous operation transmitted from millions of miles away and delayed by 3-22 minutes.\u003c/span>\u003cw:sdt id=\"260495119\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_18\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003cw:sdt id=\"-1039742604\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_19\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\"> From there, the next big challenge is making sure that the system handling autonomous operation has sufficiently high computing power and simultaneously low power consumption given much of the power consumption in the helicopter comes from a heater to keep the components warm in Martian evenings.\u003c/span> \u003cspan lang=\"EN\">Though Qualcomm Flight was not originally designed for space travel, it does have powerful autonomous operation \u003c/span>\u003cw:sdt id=\"1287011346\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_24\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">features that we believed would be a great starting point in tackling some of these upfront challenges.\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/p>\n\u003cp>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">In addition to flexible autonomous functionality, Martian radiation and atmospheric conditions were also important considerations for JPL in determining the right choice of robotics platform. Extreme temperatures and temperature cycling can wear out parts very quickly. Plus, some forms of space radiation will gradually or abruptly damage silicon. Normally, thorough testing would be ideal, along with space hardening. Through JPL’s analysis, they were able to determine that certain properties of the Qualcomm Flight technology would reduce risk of faults and would qualify the needs for the first flight on another planet.\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/p>\n"},{"type":"image","image":"https://www.qualcomm.com/sites/ember/files/styles/optimize/public/blog/managed-images/qc_onq_mars_688x444.png?itok=5k4SdHtV","class":"inline","description":"Qualcomm Flight Platform (inset) powering the Ingenuity helicopter. Image credit: NASA/JPL-Caltech","title":"","alt":"","width":688,"height":444},{"type":"html","value":"\u003ch3>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cw:sdt id=\"1475415164\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_29\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">Putting together the right \u003c/span>\u003cw:sdt id=\"1235587510\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_30\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003cw:sdt id=\"1606221822\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_31\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003cw:sdt id=\"449676310\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_32\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">toolset\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/h3>\n\u003cp>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">Qualcomm Flight was originally developed from the ground up with autonomous flight in mind. The\u003c/span> \u003cspan lang=\"EN\">platform focuses on technological benefits typically aimed at consumer drone technology, such as 4K ultra-HD video, heterogeneous mobile computing, navigation via visual inertial odometry, and flight assistance — all in an extremely small and durable package. These were all features that came to mind when JPL considered the constraints of remotely operating a helicopter on Mars, and the complex algorithms the helicopter would need to compute. Autonomous flight by a helicopter on Mars is critical to navigating areas the Rover cannot easily access and opening new possibilities for exploration, obtaining high resolution images, and more ground covered through faster travel. \u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/p>\n\u003cp>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">A major factor that helped us get a head start in our collaboration with JPL was our already extensive testing methodology for commercial technology. \u003c/span>\u003cw:sdt id=\"-903215730\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_33\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003cw:sdt id=\"1694260960\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_34\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">We’re always striving to push the limits of the technology we are developing, and it’s exciting when that enables adjacent opportunities to thrive. This streamlined the process of integrating Qualcomm Flight into JPL’s project, and exemplifies how\u003c/span>\u003cw:sdt id=\"313078743\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_35\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003cw:sdt id=\"-6604184\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_36\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\"> our highly integrated solutions and rigorous testing enables Qualcomm Technologies solutions to easily adapt to the needs of other industry segments. Qualcomm Flight would go on to not only successfully endure our own rigorous hardware testing in our own labs, it also passed JPL’s simulation tests for Mars here on Earth.\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/p>\n\u003cp>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cw:sdt id=\"-894974906\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_37\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003cw:sdt id=\"622430631\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_38\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">This project also gave us a unique opportunity to test the platform for the extreme conditions that Ingenuity would be exposed to. The testing also turned around valuable learnings that can be applied to future missions. For example, we were able to quantify for JPL how parts degraded after exposure to radiation, allowing them to model risk. This can enable JPL to decide whether or not to fly a particular mission down the line. \u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/p>\n\u003cp>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">In addition to enabling the autonomous functioning of Ingenuity, Qualcomm Flight is also used in the communication system of the Mars Rover. The computing capabilities of Qualcomm Flight on the Rover processes the photos taken by the helicopter. This allows both Ingenuity and the Rover to work in tandem to gather and prepare the best possible photos that will be sent back to the JPL team on Earth.\u003c/span>\u003cw:sdt id=\"-1108812518\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_42\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003cw:sdt id=\"-1633703028\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_43\" showingplchdr=\"t\">     \u003c/w:sdt>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/p>\n"},{"type":"youtube","id":"qwdfdE6ruMw"},{"type":"html","value":"\u003cp>Video credit: NASA Jet Propulsion Laboratory\u003c/p>\n\u003ch3>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">Better innovation through collaboration\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/h3>\n\u003cp>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">These kinds of test results could only be achieved through thoughtful collaboration and trust between Qualcomm Technologies and Qualcomm Government Technologies and JPL. The mindset from the beginning was rooted in a collaborative engagement and dialogue that enabled the involved entities to engage and learn about the environment each side operates in. \u003c/span>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">\u003cspan>Taking\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\"> a deeply empathic view of each other with an outward mindset helped unify the collective thinking in order to best overcome obstacles by use Qualcomm Flight effectively for the mission. The relationship involved technical, business and contracts teams to bring together a cross collaborative team from the entities to ensure 2-way understanding towards a solution.   \u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/p>\n\u003cp>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">Collaborating with JPL on the Mars Helicopter project has been an incredibly exciting honor and a testament to what’s possible when technology companies and end customers work together. This project will shape future technological development for space exploration utilizing commercial technology and research. It also will help drive further innovation in robotics at Qualcomm Technologies. Since the introduction of Qualcomm Flight, we have introduced other \u003c/span>\u003cw:sdt id=\"-938063523\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_59\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003ca href=\"/products/industrial-commercial/robotics\">\u003cspan>\u003cspan>Qualcomm Robotics Platforms\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/a>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">. That’s why Qualcomm Technologies, which includes Qualcomm Government Technologies and Qualcomm CDMA Technologies, is pleased to share the hard work we’ve been doing with \u003c/span>\u003ca href=\"https://www.jpl.nasa.gov/who-we-are\">\u003cspan>\u003cspan>NASA Jet Propulsion Labs (JPL)\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/a>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\"> in developing technologies and solutions that power the Mars helicopter, \u003c/span>\u003cw:sdt id=\"1847124796\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_10\">\u003ca href=\"https://www.nasa.gov/feature/jpl/nasa-s-mars-helicopter-reports-in\">\u003ci>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>Ingenuity\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/i>\u003c/a>\u003c/w:sdt>\u003ci>\u003cu>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">\u003cspan>,\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/u>\u003c/i> \u003cw:sdt id=\"-732536596\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_11\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">to prepare for the first powered flight on another planet.\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/p>\n\u003cp>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">The Mars helicopter project has been in development since 2014 and is the culmination of rigorous testing and innovation. The project is meant to be a technology demonstration by JPL to showcase how autonomous flight can expand the horizon of space exploration, research, and data\u003c/span>\u003cw:sdt id=\"1610544006\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_13\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003cw:sdt id=\"-1187675835\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_14\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\"> for future missions and designs. No technical detail would be too small to consider, including the processor that would be responsible for the helicopter’s operation.\u003c/span>\u003cw:sdt id=\"383460742\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_16\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\"> When JPL approached us about testing and expanding the autonomous capabilities of Ingenuity using products from \u003c/span>\u003cw:sdt id=\"-1331903821\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_17\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">Qualcomm Technologies, we were thrilled to share in their team’s vision. \u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/p>\n\u003ch3>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">The challenges of first-ever space flight\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/h3>\n\u003cp>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">The rigors of space pose unique challenges to operating a helicopter on Mars — challenges our \u003c/span>\u003ca href=\"/news/onq/2015/09/10/first-public-demo-snapdragon-flight-robotics-dev-platform-one-worlds-smallest-4k\">\u003cspan>\u003cspan>Qualcomm Flight Platform\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/a>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">, is capable of addressing. The main hurdle is operation itself; due to signals taking minutes to arrive, controlling a helicopter via remote control in real time is impossible. The helicopter must instead receive commands for autonomous operation transmitted from millions of miles away and delayed by 3-22 minutes.\u003c/span>\u003cw:sdt id=\"260495119\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_18\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003cw:sdt id=\"-1039742604\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_19\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\"> From there, the next big challenge is making sure that the system handling autonomous operation has sufficiently high computing power and simultaneously low power consumption given much of the power consumption in the helicopter comes from a heater to keep the components warm in Martian evenings.\u003c/span> \u003cspan lang=\"EN\">Though Qualcomm Flight was not originally designed for space travel, it does have powerful autonomous operation \u003c/span>\u003cw:sdt id=\"1287011346\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_24\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">features that we believed would be a great starting point in tackling some of these upfront challenges.\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/p>\n\u003cp>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">In addition to flexible autonomous functionality, Martian radiation and atmospheric conditions were also important considerations for JPL in determining the right choice of robotics platform. Extreme temperatures and temperature cycling can wear out parts very quickly. Plus, some forms of space radiation will gradually or abruptly damage silicon. Normally, thorough testing would be ideal, along with space hardening. Through JPL’s analysis, they were able to determine that certain properties of the Qualcomm Flight technology would reduce risk of faults and would qualify the needs for the first flight on another planet.\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/p>\n"},{"type":"image","image":"https://www.qualcomm.com/sites/ember/files/styles/optimize/public/blog/managed-images/qc_onq_mars_688x444.png?itok=5k4SdHtV","class":"inline","description":"Qualcomm Flight Platform (inset) powering the Ingenuity helicopter. Image credit: NASA/JPL-Caltech","title":"","alt":"","width":688,"height":444},{"type":"html","value":"\u003ch3>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cw:sdt id=\"1475415164\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_29\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">Putting together the right \u003c/span>\u003cw:sdt id=\"1235587510\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_30\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003cw:sdt id=\"1606221822\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_31\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003cw:sdt id=\"449676310\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_32\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">toolset\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/h3>\n\u003cp>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">Qualcomm Flight was originally developed from the ground up with autonomous flight in mind. The\u003c/span> \u003cspan lang=\"EN\">platform focuses on technological benefits typically aimed at consumer drone technology, such as 4K ultra-HD video, heterogeneous mobile computing, navigation via visual inertial odometry, and flight assistance — all in an extremely small and durable package. These were all features that came to mind when JPL considered the constraints of remotely operating a helicopter on Mars, and the complex algorithms the helicopter would need to compute. Autonomous flight by a helicopter on Mars is critical to navigating areas the Rover cannot easily access and opening new possibilities for exploration, obtaining high resolution images, and more ground covered through faster travel. \u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/p>\n\u003cp>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">A major factor that helped us get a head start in our collaboration with JPL was our already extensive testing methodology for commercial technology. \u003c/span>\u003cw:sdt id=\"-903215730\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_33\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003cw:sdt id=\"1694260960\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_34\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">We’re always striving to push the limits of the technology we are developing, and it’s exciting when that enables adjacent opportunities to thrive. Qualcomm Flight would go on to not only successfully endure our own rigorous hardware testing in our own labs, it also passed JPL’s simulation tests for Mars here on Earth.\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/p>\n\u003cp>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cw:sdt id=\"-894974906\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_37\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003cw:sdt id=\"622430631\" sdttag=\"goog_rdk_38\">\u003c/w:sdt>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">This project also gave us a unique opportunity to test the platform for the extreme conditions that Ingenuity would be exposed to. The testing also turned around valuable learnings that can be applied to future missions. For example, we were able to quantify for JPL how parts degraded after exposure to radiation, allowing them to model risk. This can enable JPL to decide whether or not to fly a particular mission down the line. \u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/p>\n\u003cp>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">In addition to enabling the autonomous functioning of Ingenuity, Qualcomm Flight is also used in the communication system of the Mars Rover. Recently, we had the opportunity to work on another important initiative: the\u003c/span> \u003ca href=\"https://cmea.georgetown.edu/studentsupportservices/community-scholars/\">\u003cspan>\u003cspan>Georgetown Community Scholars Program\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/a>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">\u003cspan>. \u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/p>\n\u003cp>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">\u003cspan>Launched more than 40 years ago, the goal of the program is to \u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">promote social justice by enrolling and supporting a more racially and socioeconomically diverse student body. \u003cspan>As an alum of Georgetown University, I’m honored that we were able to be a part of this program and help more young people access the kind of enriching higher education I was lucky to experience. The funding provided by \u003c/span>Qualcomm directly supported low-income, first-generation college students who were disproportionately impacted by technology gaps. To equip them for distance learning during the Covid-19 pandemic, we provided the students with a variety of connected devices, including laptops, webcams, headphones, and Wi-Fi hotspots.\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/p>\n\u003cp>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan>\u003cspan lang=\"EN\">It’s been great to hear about the resulting impact.
